  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

And I think if all goes well then the rest of the books will likely become movies as well. <br /><br />When it will be release is tbd. Meaning who knows when it will be out...it could take years before you finally get to see it...but that should all be worth it to make sure it gets well adapted.<br /><br />But I believe with as strict as India is with films that this will likely be banned from coming out in their country since many might find it insulting to the culture,mythology, or view of their country. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_165687986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165687986" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165687986?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781402784057" href="/book/show/12044735-tiger-s-voyage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=i-ship-it">i-ship-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165687986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15301702913669333376"><u>Warning: spoilers if you haven't read the first 2 books!</u><br/><br/>Okay, to all you who understand and share my intense love for this series, let me explain the rating. Because I <i>do</i> still love these books, and I <i>did</i> really enjoy this one, but after considering it, I just couldn't give it 5 stars.<br/><br/>First, a positive: the adventure in this book is wonderful! I feel like this is the first time that it was so good that it eclipsed the romance(s) and relationships of the characters. I was fascinated by the journe</span>
  <span id="freeText15301702913669333376" style="display:none"><u>Warning: spoilers if you haven't read the first 2 books!</u><br /><br />Okay, to all you who understand and share my intense love for this series, let me explain the rating. Because I <i>do</i> still love these books, and I <i>did</i> really enjoy this one, but after considering it, I just couldn't give it 5 stars.<br /><br />First, a positive: the adventure in this book is wonderful! I feel like this is the first time that it was so good that it eclipsed the romance(s) and relationships of the characters. I was fascinated by the journey to visit the 5 dragons and all Kelsey, Ren, and Kishan had to accomplish to retrieve the Pearl Necklace of Durga. I also really loved the dragons and the fact that everything was based just as much on Chinese folklore as Indian.<br /><br />That one of my favorite parts of this series - Houck's interweaving of so many different types of folklore into one series. I'm constantly astounded by how much research she does and all the planning she must have done before writing these books. Everything fits together seamlessly, and it's really impressive! That was my favorite part of the book this time around.<br /><br />Now, here was the rub for me: the love triangle. Don't get me wrong, I <i>love</i> a love triangle done right. The Bella/Edward/Jacob plotline in <i>Twilight</i> was great for me. I mean, my team lost, but that's become a thing for me - choosing the losing side of a love triangle. (I should join a support group or something...)<br /><br />Anyway, but I was excited in <i>Tiger's Quest</i> to see that Kishan was getting more face-time. I really enjoyed his character, and even though I loved Ren at the beginning, Kishan really won me over by the end. He was funny and charming and had less of a Superman-complex than Ren, which I often found a bit irritating.<br /><br />So when I saw that the love triangle was going to play a bigger role in Tiger's Voyage, I was excited. More Kishan! And I really enjoyed the interplay between Ren and Kishan, and their rivalry. It was funny in the last book. And I was pissed at Ren when at the end of the last book, he didn't remember Kelsey. And who was there to pick up the pieces? Kishan. I was ready for this all to come to a head in Tiger's Voyage.<br /><br />But what I found made me a little uneasy. The beginning started off good for me, with Kelsey and Ren arguing up a storm. But it was funny, and I've got to say, it was hot! Their best interaction comes when they're fighting. But I was disappointed in Kishan. He stood by and watched entirely too calmly. He lost a lot of his personality in this book. What we all loved in Quest - his cockiness, humor, and charm - were all but gone in Voyage. I hardly recognized him!<br /><br />And then the love triangle began to really take shape, and I've got to say, I was super disappointed. What we're presented with is Kelsey's connection with Ren and how all-consuming it is, and a Kishan who is the anchor that helps her keep her sanity. Kelsey soon has to decide which brother she wants to be wish, and she picks Kishan because he's stable...and we're led to believe this is a bad thing.<br /><br />I give you the following exercepts:<br /><br /><i>I thought it would be easier, more practical, if I just picked Kishan. No, practical is the wrong word. Safer. That's the right one. Ren took risks. Ren surrounded himself with beautiful bikini-clad girls. [...] I know why he did it, but the fact remains that he still did. And if another opportunity to "save me" came along, he wouldn't hesitate. He'd once again sacrifice himself, and I'd be alone. I'd almost had the man of my dreams. But almost doesn't count.<br /><br />[...]<br /><br />Besides, who took care of me when Ren nobly let himself be kidnapped? Kishan. Who told off Randi when she was insulting me? Kishan. Who lets me wear my hair the way I want to? Kishan. Who said he'd be willing to let me be with another if that's what I really wanted? Kishan. Who never argues with me? Kishan. Who kepts his hands off when I asked him to? Kishan. (p. 454-455)</i><br /><br />And this one, which really tipped me over the edge...<br /><br /><i>He [Kishan] protected me from the relationship roller coaster ride that was Ren. I loved Kishan, and I believed I could be happy with him, but I also had to acknowledge that it wasn't exactly the same. Ren's love was an all-consuming fire, but Kishan was more like...a space heater. Comfortable, steady, reliable. Both kept me warm, but one could burn me. Singe me to ashes. If Kishan left me, I would cry. I would hurt, but I would move on, sadder but wiser.<br /><br />Loving Ren was like loving an atom bomb. When he went off, and it was just a matter of time before he did again, he would destroy everything around in a ten-mile radius. Of course, I always managed to be standing in the middle of the bull's-eye. Shrapnel had mangled my heart. Twice. Kishan tried to pick up the pieces and hold them together by sheer will, but there were gaps. Pieces were missing.<br /><br />[...] I had to pick between the consuming love of Ren that I was so desperate for I sometimes forgot to breathe, and the steady glow, the endless kindness and comfort that Kishan offered me. (p. 433-434)</i><br /><br />We all know Kelsey will end up with Ren on the last page of the last book. It's a given. But Voyage left me wondering if Kelsey was crazy. Why does she love Ren more?!<br /><br />And this was where I was left with a bit of a bad taste in my mouth. Houck presents us with Kelsey and Ren's relationship, one which follows the common theme of paranormal romances, in which their love is literally the only thing that keeps them alive. Ren even declares that Kelsey is the purpose of his existence. I'm sorry, but if your significant other is the purpose of your existence, your life must be really pathetic.<br /><br />And, sure, that type of love makes for a really good, dramatic story. Why has "Romeo and Juliet" survived for so long (other than it's great one-liners)? Because it's a powerful love story of two individuals who were so in love that they couldn't survive without it. But how many people in the real world want this type of relationship?<br /><br />Umm...no thanks.<br /><br />To me, Kishan represented a healthy sort of love. He was supportive and devoted, but he had other things going on in his life. He didn't practically worship at Kelsey's feet like Ren did. And while Kelsey was attached to him, she could think of other things when he was around. As opposed to her relationship with Ren, which is practically a drug.<br /><br />It was all very teenage angsty and annoying.<br /><br />And this was what kept me from giving this book 5 stars. I'm just not with Houck on portraying this type of all-encompassing, obsessive sort of love to teens, who already think everything is the end of the world. It reminded me too much of Bella's willingness to kill herself when Edward left. While Kelsey isn't as bad as Bella, she's still tempted by that connection with Ren that will make her lose herself. And because I'm positive that she and Ren will end up together, I'm a little miffed.<br /><br />Maybe I'm wrong. Maybe their love with tone down a bit. Maybe she'll even pick Kishan in the end.<br /><br />...but I doubt it.<br /><br />Am I the only one that thinks the relationship Kelsey and Ren share is not only not normal but not healthy? It took me almost a week to get through this book because I was disappointed. And even though I adored the adventure and the mythology, and did like some of the romance, I just was a little uncomfortable with the turn the story took and some of the themes.<br /><br /><b>Am I crazy for thinking this? What is everyone else's thoughts?</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15301702913669333376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601760453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17318177753774354039"><b>First opinion after finish reading:</b><br/><br/>Zero star for bastardizing Hindu and Chinese myths, taking mythical figures out of context, giving them entirely unrealistic backstories and twisting them into some unrecognizable creatures. Negative star for giving untrue and unreliable information about foreign myth and culture to the audience.<br/><br/>The silly, *unbearable* love triangle and the childish, airhead 'heroine' also got a big thumb down from me. I'm equally not amused by the fact that almost every single</span>
  <span id="freeText17318177753774354039" style="display:none"><b>First opinion after finish reading:</b><br><br>Zero star for bastardizing Hindu and Chinese myths, taking mythical figures out of context, giving them entirely unrealistic backstories and twisting them into some unrecognizable creatures. Negative star for giving untrue and unreliable information about foreign myth and culture to the audience.<br><br>The silly, *unbearable* love triangle and the childish, airhead 'heroine' also got a big thumb down from me. I'm equally not amused by the fact that almost every single man in the story seems to be in love/lust with our Mary Sue 'heroine'.<br><br><b> detailed rant starts from here:</b><br><br>After finished reading Tiger's Voyage, I know I have a bone to pick with its creator: Colleen Houck.<br> <br>After suffering three books, now I think the only way for this series to work out well is for the whole setting to be pushed back into the ancient India, just so that the whole idea about princes got turned into animals by evil doers, girls being chosen to break the curse and goddesses came down to chat with mortals can be passably viewed as "normal". <br><br>But you can hardly do all these things in the * modern* American society and the *modern* Indian society and expects us to swallow the whole thing down without any skepticism. Not when the whole idea isn't even finely excised. <br><br>But of course Houck wouldn't have it that way. For one thing, if the story takes place in ancient India, then the heroine has to be an Indian or at least, an Asian girl as well, for how likely could you find a Westerner girl in the ancient India anyway? <br><br>And I also think I know why Houck wouldn't have it:<br><br>(a) she isn't able to write an Asian girl as a heroine. Because an empty-headed, immature American teenage girl is much, much easier to write.<br> <br>(b) Putting the story back to ancient India would request a lot and a lot of research on historical details, which I'm sure wouldn't sit well with Houck. <br><br>Just for the record. After reading three books, I had a burning question awaited some answer:<br><br><b>Question: Has Colleen Houck ever set one foot upon India before, during, after she wrote the Tiger series?</b><br><br>I strongly suspect that the answer to this question is 'No'. Or maybe she did visit India at some point, but her ability of observation is so BAD that a lot of things about India--the country, the people, the society and even the <i>weather</i>, simply escape her notice. <br><br>Why would I say that? Let me give you an example here: In book 1, Kelsey visited India for the first time, and she never mentioned seeing any poor people, or one single beggar on the street.<br><br>I'm sorry? No poor people and no beggar in sight?<br><br> It's not realistic for the poors to be nowhere in sight in India. As sad as it sounds, beggars are part of the scenery in every single Indian city, town and spot of tourist attraction, and everywhere you go, sign of poverty always shows up at the corners of your eyes. But no, Kelsey made it sound like every single person who lived in India was rich or at the very least, middle class. <br><br>Plus, I hate it very much that the 'good' princes never lifted a finger to help the poors and misfortunes in India with their wealth. My freaking goodness!<br><br>Not only this, Kelsey barely made comment on how hot the weather is in India, and not once did she seem to notice the social barriers between men and women. <br><br>I admit all of these are just small details, but after seeing Houck failed to handle all of these small details well, her books become very unrealistic in my eyes. <br><br>After asking my question, now I will go down to the rant. I need to list down everything I HATE about Tiger's Voyage.<br><br>Here we go.<br><br><b>1.The unbearable 'heroine' and her stupid, unrealistic love interests</b><br><br>Throughout the three books, Kelsey acted like an airhead teenager, and I see no improvement or character growth in sight.<br><br>And yes, Kelsey is a big fat Mary Sue too. Aside from the two handsome princes who were totally in love with her, every single man in the series--even the ARCH VILLAIN, is also in love/lust with her. And in book 3, even the *male* dragons seem to like her, for no good reason.<br><br>Plus, Houck, along with the two princes, keep telling me how brave and wonderful Kelsey is though out the book, but sadly all I can see is Kelsey having to be rescued constantly, and almost every risky task is performed by the two tiger brothers, instead of our GREAT BRAVE KELSEY.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419326i/831167.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Talking about the two tiger brothers. Ren continues to be a cardboard cutout Prince Charming, who rants about Kelsey cutting off her hair. Oh yes, he doesn't like her short hair. But It's her hair and she can do whatever she feels like, for goodness' sake! <br><br>Kishan is slightly better than Ren, but for the life in me, after so many books I still can't see why he is in love with Kelsey. Full Stop.<br><br><b>2. The horrible love triangle</b><br><br>In book 3, Ren somehow lost his memory to Kelsey and and he subconsciously wanted to stay away from her.<br><br>My reaction is: "REN! IF YOUR SUBCONSCIOUSNESS IS TRYING TO TELL YOU SOMETHING, LISTEN TO IT! IT IS FOR YOUR OWN GOOD!!!"<br><br>After Ren's losing his memory, a huge part of the book is taken up by Kelsey moving back and froth between Kishan and Ren, and Ren being jealous of Kishan or some random guy who was interested in Kelsey.<br><br>We run repeatedly to the old problem: Every single man wants Kelsey, no kidding. <s>even the bad guy wants to bed her. YUCK!</s><br><br>In the middle of the mess, Ren went all "Let's break up with Kelsey for her own good!"---all Edward Cullen's style! Fucking hell! Give me a fucking break! This "I'm-ditching-you-for-your-own-good" BS is annoying as hell! <br><br>When I was turning the last twenty pages of the book, it was confirmed that Kelsey didn't lift a finger to do any difficult task, she never had to take any risk because the tiger brothers would do all her bidding for her.<br><br>WHAT HAD THE BROTHERS EVER DONE WRONG IN THEIR MISERABLE PAST LIVES TO DESERVE THIS!?<br><br><b>3. Total bastardization of the Hindu and Chinese myths</b><br><br>After reducing Warrior Goddess Durga into a lame Disney style of a fairy godmother (I mean, the Goddess never lifted a finger to punish the evil doers, for crying out loud!). Colleen Houck continues to butcher the Hindu myth in Tiger's Voyage. <br><br>But this time the Hindu myth isn't her only victim, the Chinese traditional myth also suffers, just as badly. <br><br>First, let me tell you about what had happened to the good ol' Hindu myth. <br><br>At one point, a character tells a 'myth' about Shiva, Pravati and Indra <b>in a love triangle</b>. WHAT!? WHAT? WHAT? WHERE DID THIS 'MYTH' COME FROM!?<br><br>Just for the record, I had never came across with a tale about Indra, or any male deity messing about with Pravati. The point is according to Hindu myth, NO ONE MESSES WITH PRAVATI OR THEY WILL SUFFER SHIVA'S WRATH. That's it.<br><br>Just for the record, there is a myth about Rama's wife Sita being kidnapped by a Demon King, who fell in lust with Sita, <i>but this myth is about Rama and Sita, not about Pravati, Shiva and Indra.</i><br><br>Also, according to Houck, Shiva ordered his 'servant' Nandi to transform into a shark for one stupid reason or the other. But she never bothers to tell you Nandi is in fact Shiva's cow in the myth.<br><br>Nandi, you're so ruined.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419327i/831168.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Colleen Houck also has the gut to claim that Pravati is the other name of Durga. <i>I'm sorry, isn't it the other way around?</i> That Durga is the other name of Pravati? That Durga is Pravati's warrior form? <br><br>And why it's never mentioned that Durga became Kali when she was enraged during a great battle with a demon?<br><br>And why, for three whole books, no one ever mentioned the belief about Pravati, Durga and all the other goddesses are in fact one and the same, Devi?<br><br>But at least I have to give a small credit to Houck for mentioning the Hindu goddesses and their ever-changing appearance, personalities and moods are not very different from what mortal women are being. <br><br>Secondly, let's move on to see what had happened with the Chinese myth.<br><br>At one point of the story, a Captain told Kelsey of a supposed Chinese myth about Jingwei. The Captain claimed that Jingwei was once a woman, whose husband drowned at sea, after the death of her husband, the woman became a bird out of grief.<br><br>Well, I have to tell you Houck had the details all wrong here. Every single 10 years old Han Chinese kid who had read <i>Chinese Myths For Kids</i> can tell you the correct version of the myth: Jingwei was once the daughter of Emperor Yandi, who was drowned as a young girl, after her death, her spirit transformed itself into a bird. (More details about the myth of Jingwei: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jingwei">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jingwei</a>) <br><br>I am serious, every single 10 years old Han Chinese kids knows the story of Jingwei, and I bet everyone who had bothered enough to pick up a <i>Beginners' Guide To Chinese Mythology</i> and read, would also know the story. So tell me Houck, how could you mess this up so badly?<br><br><b>4. All the messed up little details...</b><br><br><i>(a) Indians celebrate a Chinese festival. Are you for real?</i> <br><br>At one point, Ren and Kishan took Kelsey to attempt a festival, which Houck called it 'Stars Festival', claiming it's a festival imported from China during the ancient period, and had been celebrated by the Indian general public ever since.<br><br>I died a little when I saw this wild claim. <br><br>I know this supposed Star Festival well, in China we called it Double Seventh Festival, aka Chinese Valentine's Day (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Seventh">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_S...</a>). The Festival celebrates the yearly union of The Weaver Girl and The Cowherd, two figures in the Chinese myths, who were only allowed to meet each other once a year at the night of the seventh day of the 7th lunar month. <br><br>I also know that <b>only Chinese, Japanese and Koreans celebrate Double Seventh Festival</b>, as to the Indians, this Festival isn't part of their traditional calendar. <br><br>Just to be on the safe side, I also looked up the Wiki's list of Hindu Festivals (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Hindu_festivals">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_...</a>), only to confirm that there's no such thing as believers of Hinduism celebrating a festival imported from China, which is related to stars.<br><br>I find it truly disgusting, for what Houck had committed here isn't some slight mistake or misunderstanding. People, listen up. <b>Colleen Houck is feeding you untrue information about foreign culture and myths here.</b> She made things up, presenting her make-believes as <i>facts</i> and feeding them to her readers. She <i>lies</i>. From this point onward I know that everything she wrote in her books are not to be trusted, not without a double check. <br><br>To be frank, I had never encountered an 'author' who is so <b>SHAMELESS and DISRESPECTFUL</b> before.<br><br><i>(b) mention of cheongsam...but something doesn't look right</i><br><br>Plus, during the festival; Kelsey was dressed up in a blue cheongsam. According to Houck's description, Kelesy was being dressed like the following photo during a festival: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinese_woman_in_Qipao.jpg/328px-Chinese_woman_in_Qipao.jpg">http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419327i/831169._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Most likely it's the type of Cheongsam you would only see in seedy nightclubs and pervert's wetdreams. *facepalms*<br><br>This cheongsam business also leads me to another messed up little detail...<br><br><i>(c) Ren and Kishan's mother...a supposed cheongsam-wearing Chinese woman from 300 years ago?</i><br><br>First thing, let me tell you what cheongsam used to look like from 300 years ago, I took the picture from Wiki:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381150585i/4383533._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, I don't think Ren and Kishan's mother would be comfortable wearing clothes like this when she lived in India.<br><br>When I was reading book 1 and book 2, the thought about Ren and Kishan's mother being Chinese/Korean/Japanese never crossed my mind. <br><br>But when Houck mentioned about Ren's mother celebrating Double Seventh Festival and dressed herself in cheongsam even after being married to Ren and Kishan's father, I was finally forced to realize Colleen Houck has intended Ren's mother to be a Chinese born woman. That's where the problem began.<br><br>Before that, I never thought that Ren's mother was supposed to be Chinese, because her name sounded barely anything like a Chinese name, allso because Colleen Houck had mentioned that Ren had blue eyes, and Kishan's eyes are golden.<br><br>What? How come a Chinese mother and an Indian father can produce a son with BLUE EYES!? I guess the chance of it is very, very slim.<br><br><b>5. The dragons</b><br><br>Houck's dragons are...in one word, laughable. They're comical laughing stocks. I suggest you to see for yourself, I don't even want to bother with them here. And of course, powerful beings such as dragons can only be *male*, since women aren't supposed to be powerful, even supposedly powerful women like Durga, actually did nothing aside from sitting there smiling and be beautiful.<br><br> Actually I have more things to say, but this rant is getting ways too long, I will stop it here. Thank you for reading, folks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17318177753774354039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9016802348307993968"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/><i>This review contains <b>unmarked spoilers</b>, and will be redone soon.</i><br/><br/>It hurts my heart to write this review, but it must be done. TIGER'S VOYAGE ruined my complete view of the series, and you're about to learn why.<br/><br/>I used to be obsessed with this series. It was my first paranormal romance young-adult, and I credit this book for introducing me to the genre. Gradually, as I read more books, I learned the series wasn't as good as I originally though, but I still liked it.<br/><br/>However, in this book, Kelsey </span>
  <span id="freeText9016802348307993968" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br><br><i>This review contains <b>unmarked spoilers</b>, and will be redone soon.</i><br><br>It hurts my heart to write this review, but it must be done. TIGER'S VOYAGE ruined my complete view of the series, and you're about to learn why.<br><br>I used to be obsessed with this series. It was my first paranormal romance young-adult, and I credit this book for introducing me to the genre. Gradually, as I read more books, I learned the series wasn't as good as I originally though, but I still liked it.<br><br>However, in this book, Kelsey is - if possible - more annoying, stupid, and boring than ever. She's a damsel-in-distress, in the most pathetic way possible. <br><br>She almost <i>dies</i> because she <i>hits her head on a rock</i>. All because a harmless <i>eel</i> swims past her and she freaks the freak out. There was no use for the scene except to make the boys fight over her more.<br><br>WHAT IS WRONG WITH YOU, KESLEY? I can go on and on about this shallow girl. What do Kishan and Ren see in her in this book?<br><br>She's always talking or laughing to herself (when she's not even faintly amusing, mind you) or thinking PARAGRAPHS - long, detailed, dull paragraphs that clarified that somewhere in her tiny brain, a screw is loose. Seriously. And all she does is moan and groan and bitch about who she's gonna chose . . . Ren or Kishan, her moon and her shadow, her bad boy and her good boy, her first love and her replacement...<br><br>I liked Kishan better then Ren, but he lost the his badboy-appeal and his hilarious perverted comments, just to change for Kelsey. Ever heard of the original LITTLE MERMAID, Kishan? Changing herself for the prince she was biggest mistake the mermaid ever made.<br><br>I still love Kishan, though. In this book, Ren is selfish, possessive, cruel, and annoying. This "connection" he has with Kelsey annoys me to no end.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kingsley%20gifs/patsypoutusXxX/Gifs/kingsleygif7.gif?o=7" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/303497.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>TIGER'S VOYAGE contains about <b>one hundred pages</b> on details. Useless descriptions of yachts, plants, bathrooms, Ren... what not. Lord, if you think we needed the serious background info, just give us a link. I thought I was reading a young adult PNR, not my dad's marine mechanic log. <br><br>I know Kadam likes all things modern, but give me a break. I was falling asleep.<br><br>The writing is so detailed and flowery I'd choke on it if it was a perfume.<br><br>The plot was fine, though I preferred TIGER'S QUEST. The romance was terrible. I mean, we <i>all know</i> Kelsey is going to end up with Ren. It's so obvious. You can spare us the idiotic love triangle and get on with her quest, 'cause we all know her "love for Kishan" won't be enough".<br><br>Please stop.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/stop%20gifs/kelsey_baby19/gifs/juststop.gif?o=16" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380353443ra/706795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You're going to hurt Kishan.</span>

<div id="review_140237165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140237165" />
    <a title="Erica (storybookend)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2835464-erica-storybookend"><img alt="Erica (storybookend)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595779045p2/2835464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140237165?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica (storybookend)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica (storybookend)" href="/user/show/2835464-erica-storybookend">Erica (storybookend)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781402784057" href="/book/show/12044735-tiger-s-voyage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=release-in-2011">release-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=i-recommend-it">i-recommend-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=would-love-if-it-were-a-movie">would-love-if-it-were-a-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=unbearable-cliffhangers">unbearable-cliffhangers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=favorite-romance">favorite-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=incredible">incredible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140237165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4425004918602406826">Tiger’s Voyage captured my heart, ensnared my soul, and left me breathless and so so in love. I love this book, this series, with a passionate, heart soaring, brilliant love that consumes me, and I become so invested in the story and Kelsey and Ren and Kishan’s lives that their pain is my pain, their love my love, and I dread the end, because it means I must finish this part of their story, and wait, and wait, for the next part. And Colleen Houck doesn’t give you a happy, perfect ending to stay </span>
  <span id="freeText4425004918602406826" style="display:none">Tiger’s Voyage captured my heart, ensnared my soul, and left me breathless and so so in love. I love this book, this series, with a passionate, heart soaring, brilliant love that consumes me, and I become so invested in the story and Kelsey and Ren and Kishan’s lives that their pain is my pain, their love my love, and I dread the end, because it means I must finish this part of their story, and wait, and wait, for the next part. And Colleen Houck doesn’t give you a happy, perfect ending to stay your anxiety, no, she, the evil witch she is, slams the worst of cliffhangers into your face, and you turn the last page to find it blank, and you’re so desperate to find out what happens, but that’s it. That’s the ending, and you must wait, for <i>eternity</i>, to find what happens next. For this reason, I hate her. And yet I love her because she writes such a fantastic story with possibly my favorite romance that I have read. And that is because of Ren. The drop dead gorgeous, tall dark and handsome, Indian Prince of ultimate perfection. Not that he doesn’t have his faults, because he does, but there is no man who has me swooning more, than he. <br><br>I loved how dragons were incorporated into the story. That Kelsey and her two tigers had to find five dragons that would eventually lead them to Durga’s Necklace, which would bestow upon Ren and Kishan more time that they can be humans. Each of the dragons were unique and interesting. I thought the development and execution of the plot was excellent. There was adventure and danger and fantasy and heart stopping romance and laughter. One of my favorite parts was when the trio met the dragon that wanted to play a game with them that turned out to be like an old fantasy story with knights and dragons and princesses. I thought it was fantastic ;)<br><br>Now the romance. Oh my, the romance! Never has any romance been so sweltering hot and swooning inducing than what goes on between Ren and Kelsey. Every time Ren stepped onto the page and said something, or did something, or kissed or touched Kelsey, or Houck described what he was <i>wearing</i>, I was swooning, and falling for him hard. Which was like every other page. And he’s not even real! Yeesh Erica, get a grip. He is my dream man, next to Apollus in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41229-tennis-shoes" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tennis Shoe Series</a>, and all my classic men crushes. (If I had to choose between Ren and Apollus, I don’t know who I would choose. Because Apollus, strapping young Roman soldier with a strong spirit and <i>so incredibly</i> good looking, come on!) *pause as I fan myself from all the hotness going on here* <br><br><a href="http://s1216.photobucket.com/albums/dd373/PixieDT/?action=view&amp;current=ca.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343942i/699086.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/tangled%20gif/angel_kurikura/Television%20and%20Movies/Disney/flynnsmolder.gif?o=40" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a><br><br>Anywho, where was I? I also like Kishan in this novel. I liked him more in Tiger’s Quest, where he was more himself: roguish, charming, bad boy that he is. In Tiger’s Voyage his personality is watered down some, but I think he’s showing the more tender, calmer side of him who truly loves Kelsey. It shows us a different side of him that lets us understand his love and devotion to Kelsey, and that he won't take her from something that she desperately wants, even if that means giving her up to Ren. <br><br>I don’t usually like love triangles. It’s just a way for authors to add words to their story, and angst and kisses with two different guys and bemoaning of the girl that she loves them both and she can’t choose who she wants to be with, blah blah blah. <br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/tangled%20gifs/kaworu_chan/Gifs/tumblr_ld86p6gzlP1qc5807o1_500.gif?o=62" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380343942ra/699088.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But here, <i>here</i> is love triangle that I can say tops every one of those contrived romances, and soars above with stark emotion and true love that wraps around my heart and <i>I love it</i>. I love the two men vying for Kelsey’s heart, I love the changes she inspires in them, I love the sizzling moments and beautiful moments Ren and Kelsey have, I love the sweet tender moments Kelsey and Kishan have. I know there are people who don’t like it, who don’t like Kelsey and the decisions she makes, and who found something lacking in Ren and Kishan in this novel. And I understand that, and at times agree. I wish Kelsey and Ren could just be together already, and I wish that Kishan could find someone who he can come to love more than Kelsey, and realize that Kelsey will always be happier with Ren than with him. It cuts my heart to see Kishan suffer, but Ren and Kelsey are meant to be together. I think it’s time for the love triangle to stop. I hope that in <i>Tiger’s Destiny</i>, Kelsey finally firmly decides to stay with Ren forever, no matter what, though doing it gently and lovingly so that Kishan isn’t crushed.<br><br>And I’ve got to say that I loved Wes. I loved that Colleen put him into the story. He was sweet and charming, and wasn’t vying for Kelsey (though he kind of pretended to), but he still managed to put both of Kelsey’s overprotective tigers at unease and in modes of jealousy. I loved it :)<br><br>I guess these books are just my guilty pleasure. I’ll love them no matter what happens, (although if Kishan dies I <i>will</i> destroy the book. After I’ve read it all and loved the rest of it, that is.) I can understand why people don’t like these books, two of my sisters hate them for the same reasons. The writing, Kelsey’s bad decisions, the love triangle. But those things don’t bother me as much as they do most people. I feel the writing is getting better. I feel that Kelsey is growing, and learning, and becoming a stronger person. I may not have made some of the same choices she made, but I can understand her, can understand the dilemma she’s in, that the love of her life doesn’t know her, and she has this other incredible man who loves her, who is waiting for her. I have no idea what that could possibly feel like. As if you’ve lost the man you love, though he’s standing right in front of you. Though I think that I would never let him go, no matter if he doesn’t remember or want me, and I would fight to the world’s end to have him again. But that’s just me. <br><br>I just can’t help but love these books to death. They are treasures in my treasure chest of most beloved books. I don’t expect people to understand my love of them, which is perfectly fine, because I sometimes don’t understand the love people have of other books. To each their own, right? But let it be known I will always love these books, and I see Colleen as a wonderfully gifted storyteller.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4425004918602406826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9038727969031240383" style="display:none">Tiger's Voyage, the third book in the Tiger's Curse series, is amazing! I couldn't put it down! It's about 100 pages longer than Tiger's Quest and I tore through it twice as fast. <br /><br />We follow Kelsey, Ren, and Kishan who embark on their third voyage to break the Tiger's Curse. This time they travel by ocean searching for Durga's necklace. But, Ren is still suffering from his amnesia while Kishan seems to be falling more in love with Kelsey. Their voyage requires the help of five enchanting Chinese dragons and of course are being hunted by a number of undersea creatures which include a kraken. Oh yea and don't forget Lokesh who is still after them. Lots of action with tons of suspense and of course the romance. Tiger's Voyage will not let us fans of the series down.</span>

<div id="review_664391346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/664391346" />
    <a title="kiwi kili" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4470589-kiwi-kili"><img alt="kiwi kili" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364247317p2/4470589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/664391346?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kiwi kili" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kiwi kili" href="/user/show/4470589-kiwi-kili">kiwi kili</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who want to break the record for long lives. You will laugh THAT hard...</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=cutsie-chick-flick">cutsie-chick-flick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=lolz-it-ain-t-good">lolz-it-ain-t-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=man-harem">man-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=capslocks-no">capslocks-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=love-wrecktangle">love-wrecktangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=extend-your-life">extend-your-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=villain-issues">villain-issues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer664391346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4021109602220430232">Okay. So, I guess I should explain why I bothered to read this third book. See, my lovely cousin Abby read my review on the second book and thought it was hilarious. So she got all four books from her library and started reading them. And every once in a while she would start laughing like a demon. So...I needed to know. What could be SO COLOSSALLY BAD about this book that made her laugh and slam the book shut?<br/><br/>I hate unsatisfied curiosity. <br/><br/>And now I know. Am I a better person for it? Probably no</span>
  <span id="freeText4021109602220430232" style="display:none">Okay. So, I guess I should explain why I bothered to read this third book. See, my lovely cousin Abby read my review on the second book and thought it was hilarious. So she got all four books from her library and started reading them. And every once in a while she would start laughing like a demon. So...I needed to know. What could be SO COLOSSALLY BAD about this book that made her laugh and slam the book shut?<br><br>I hate unsatisfied curiosity. <br><br>And now I know. Am I a better person for it? Probably not. Probably worse for it. But am I better writer from it? <br><br>Well. Now I know what NOT to do. <br><br>Time to begin EVERYTHING WRONG WITH <b>"TIGER'S VOYAGE"</b><br><br>With Spoilers<br><br>Duh<br><br>Let's start with the biggest problem:<br><br><br><b> 1.) THE PLOT:</b> So, they need to find these items for Durga in order to break the curse, right? Right. So now they need Durga's necklace. Fine. Whatever. Want to know how they FIND said necklace? Well, only a certain dragon knows where it is. We'll call him BOSS dragon, because I don't feel like writing all of their names out with the little accents and whatever. So, they talk to this dragon's brother. Who tells them where a 2nd dragon they need to visit who will tell them where the 3rd dragon is who will tell them where the 4th dragon is who will tell them where a 5th dragon is who will tell them where the BOSS dragon is. <br><br>But wait. It gets better. So, BOSS dragon tells them where a key is. They get the key, which gets them the necklace. Happy days. Then Kelsey gets kidnapped, the end. In between these "major events" fill in with long montages of Ren and Kishan declaring their undying love to Kelsey. Well...more on that later. I'll let you know when we get there. <br><br>O.Kay. Weird. So...IS there a plot? <br><br>Guess not. <br><br><br><b>2.) KELSEY (AND HER EGO):</b> Problem the first--can it get any bigger? For a supposedly "average" girl, she certainly has a lot of sections of the book for her to tell us how GORGEOUS she looks. Cuz I guess that's really relevant to the plot. Also...Kelsey's clothes...Does anyone else have to stop for a few minutes to try and unsuccessfully figure out what the heck she's wearing? I eventually just gave up and kept reading. Or I googled whatever italicized word she randomly had in there. <br><br>Also...how can you not recognize yourself in the mirror multiple times in a row? You'd think after the first time of "not recognizing yourself" you'd be a little more open to surprise. And what is the purpose of these random "Kelsey's dressed up by magic" montages? Seriously, the bit where the dragon makes her hair grow and dresses her up or whatever for fun...that was just NOT NECESSARY. Neither was the bit where Kelsey is dressed up as Parvati. Or the bit where Kelsey gets dressed up in event a, b, c, d, e, f, whatever, you get it. <br><br>Kelsey, as everyone knows, is just plain annoying. She plays around with both Ren and Kishan's feelings because she "doesn't want to hurt either of them" or whatever, but I hope she realizes that the longer she strings Kishan along, the more it was bound to hurt when the truth all comes out. Well. <i>That's</i> gonna come back to hurt ya later. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428718ra/858095.gif" width='480"' height='360"' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Plus, what is with Ren and Kishan being so dang determined to love this crazy girl? Kelsey describes herself as pudgy, brown-haired, and plain. So...two hot Indian guys who are over 200 years old just randomly fall in love with that sort of girl? And don't tell me it's her personality. Just...don't. Don't go there. Apparently, Kelsey's 19. But she acts like she's 15, so...you know. She takes EVERYTHING to heart, and get's hurt by the smallest little things (both physically and emotionally). I can't BELIEVE that it never occurred to her that Ren's "forgetting her" was done in order to protect her. Seriously? I think everyone reading the book (and their annoying siblings reading over their shoulders) saw <b>that</b> one coming, <i>KELLS</i>. <br><br>And another thing. Kells. Am I the only person really irritated by a) Kelsey's name and b) Kelsey's nickname and c) Kelsey's millions of Indian nicknames? Please tell me I'm not alone. Am I? AM I? Seriously, if I am, I need someone to just tell me already. Don't leave me in this agony for so long. <br><br>And...Kelsey's apparent genius. I don't know if I'm the only one who noticed this...but I guess Kelsey's the only person who can figure out ANYTHING plot relevant in the series. Even though Mr. Kadam is the one going around with hundreds of years of experience and is doing all this research, Kelsey will just walk in the room and be like "oh THAT's what we need to do/find/where we need to go!". Cuz she's the amazing Kelsey. Fear her. <br><br>No, really, run away. Be afraid. Be VERY afraid. <br><br>Anyways. We'll move on. I think I've covered everything else that irritates me about Kelsey in the other review I wrote (her hair braiding? And Ren's obsession with said braids? Weird....and the ribbons. Just...the ribbons. I'm sorry <i>Kells</i>, but every time you mention putting your hair into two braids with ribbons, I think of Pippi Longstocking. Not a 19-year-old girl trying to look mature. Jus' sayin'. <br><br>Also...her hair randomly growing back. Clearly this just happened to make Ren happy. Seriously. It wasn't necessary except for that whole bit with Ren getting angry about her cutting her hair. <br><br>Also. Him getting angry about her cutting her hair...Isn't it HER hair, <s>Edward</s>? I mean....REN. Whoops. How did I make THAT mistake?<br><br><br><b>3.) THE MEN AND THE (OTHER) WOMEN:</b> So...apparently everyone in Ms. Houck's world is gorgeous. Because that's how Kelsey seems to describe them all. In her mind, EVERYONE is good-lookin'. She's jealous of EVERY girl because they ALL try to push each other over in order to get to Ren and Kishan. <br><br>(Snicker. Sorry, the mental imagery is just too much for me to handle.)<br><br>Randi is annoying, blond, stupid, anorexic**, and a cliche. An overly used cliche that apparently Ren thought he should use to try and make Kelsey jealous. What IS it with female authors now-a-days who think they need to have a bitchy blond girl character to pick on their poor, plain, brunette heroine? Seriously, this is just getting on my nerves now. Is it possible to NOT use cliches and get a point across? Please? Can we? Randi is an awful person, fine whatever. But she was also completely unnecessary to the plot. <br><br>(**Aside: Please, please, PLEASE stop using "anorexic bitchy popular girls" as a way to make your heroine more "heroic" for "eating normally". Anorexia is a serious mental illness that affects millions of men and women worldwide and, at its worst, can cause DEATH. This is NOT the message you want to send young impressionable girls, especially since, contrary to popular belief, anorexia is not caused by "seeing too many thin models in magazines and TV" but is actually uneven brain chemistry. People with anorexia LITERALLY CANNOT HELP IT. Their struggles are real and their stories are often very sad. To see all that thrown away for the sake of another boring YA heroine puff herself up for being "bigger than most girls" is the worst skinny-shaming I've ever seen. <br><br>STOP. IT.<br><br>STOP MARGINALIZING SERIOUS MENTAL HEALTH CONCERNS. <br><br>Thank you.)<br><br>And all you authors out there? Enough with the <s>Bella</s> Mary Sue girl characters, would you? We really don't need a bunch of "I'm a badass man-lover" brunettes running around in random pieces of clothing I can't even bother to pronounce let alone begin to understand what they mean (not because I'm opposed to learning about new cultures, but because Houck almost does these name drops to "impress upon us" how much googling she did). Enough with the cliches, please. If I can complain about them any more, I will. They are generally used by inexperienced authors and, sadly, they are being accepted by people if Houck's gettin' rich off of stupid people who love cliches. This is a bad lesson to teach an author (give them a bloated head, why doncha) and a bad lesson to teach teenage girls. Real life isn't like that at ALL. <br><br>Welcome to the real world. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428718i/858096.jpg" width="320" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If we can get a decent heroine in modern fiction who I do not despise, that person gets a happy face sticker on their review. Serious.<br><br>Anyways, back to the problem with the OTHER WOMEN here...Again, all gorgeous. Again, even Nilima is a source of jealousy. Seriously? I PITY Nilima. That poor girl is seriously just a plot device who shows up when she's important and then disappears again. I actually stopped reading at one point and asked my cousin "wait....is Nilima even on the yacht?" Apparently, she was. I found that out later when she was randomly inserted back into the plot. Also, apparently she was fasting because of some random reason or another that somehow justifies her being gone for previous chapters. <br><br>And now for the men. <br><br>The men. <br><br>The men. <br><br>Oh dear. <br><br>Is every man in the world in love with Kelsey? Well, let's see so far:<br><br>1. Ren. Fine. ONE love interest. <br><br>2. Kishan. His brother. Why? Soap opera much?<br><br>3. Li. Is there a reason here?<br><br>4. Jason and Artie. Because apparently it's now socially acceptable to date multiple guys at once.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428718ra/858097.gif" width="480" height="456" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5. Texan diving instructor guy. Because I guess we can only get a 21-year-old diving instructor randomly in India. Ya know. Instead of an old veteran who would NOT become another love interest. Or...love toy, really, because they're very clear that he's not a love INTEREST, he's just there to compliment her and make her boyfriends happy. <br><br>Like a slave. <br><br>Whoops, did I say that out loud?<br><br>6. Lokesh. Yep. Lokesh. I'll get back to that later. (Surprised, aren't you? Have to flip back to the book and remember WHO Lokesh is again, don't you? Because you forgot that there was supposed to be a villain in these books. That's okay. I did too.)<br><br>Also, the men in general...how many times do they have to grunt? Because they seem to do that a LOT. Just go back and count. It is ridiculous. <br><br><br><b>4.) LET'S DESTROY YEARS OF CULTURE AND HISTORY TIME!!! YAY!!!:</b> Okay, so I'm not the first person to point this out, but Houck has a strange obsession with giving us RANDOM INFO DUMP THAT YOU DIDN'T WANT TO KNOW!!! sections. And the best bit? Well, in an attempt to tell us how much research she's done, Houck has actually shown me how LITTLE research she's done. Because she's destroyed a lot of history and culture in an attempt to fit it into her book. <br><br>First off, a lot of these sections are just randomly put into the story. No, I'm serious. They just have little "TELL ME A STORY!!" times that have no plot relevance whatsoever. If I WANTED to read a history book, I'd BUY a history book. And I have before. It's been done. First, Houck does not accurately portray Durga or Parvati. I had to study a lot of Indian myths and culture in Honors English class and if the goddess she's talking about is supposed to be the same goddess in those myths....there's something wrong here. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428718ra/858098.gif" width="500" height="298" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also. Gilgamesh. Yeah, I know that she talks about it in the 2nd book, not the 3rd one, but I don't have room to do it on the other review. The story of Gilgamesh is actually about Gilgamesh turning into a jack-a** into a nice dude after he accidentally kills his friend Enkidu and then fails to bring him back to life. It has little to do with Gilgamesh being "clever" or about him sneaking into the realm of the gods or snakes shedding their skin. Really Kelsey? Snakes shedding their skin? How did you get THAT out of the epic poem of Gilgamesh? And no, I didn't label it an epic, that's actually what it's called. <br><br>TOO EPIC FOR YOU KELSEY. You didn't embrace the show not tell law. Shame on you. Kill it with fire and all that. The only way the word "epic" could be used to describe this book is if the word "fail" came after it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428718ra/858099.gif" width="180" height="248" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>EPIC FAIL</b><br><br><br><b>5.) LOVE MONTAGES:</b> I don't think Ren is really her boyfriend. I think he's a guy she hired to give her compliments. You think I'm joking? I'm not. It's almost as bad as watching Kristen Stewart say "I LOVE you Edward" as angrily and forcefully as she can. Kelsey, if you have to hear a guy tell you he loves you a million times in order to believe him, then maybe....just maybe...you're making a mistake here. You're 19 years old. Possibly, there will be other men out there. You've already proven THAT. Possibly you should wait a few years before trying to get married right away?<br><br>And let me just remind everyone the one big pervert similarity between this and Twilight: they are hundreds of years old. She's 19. Creepy much? And no, it's not okay to say "BUT THEY WERE TIGERS ALL THOSE YEARS!!" Do you think I care? No. Just...no. They want to marry her that's disgusting, really. Almost as bad as what's coming up next....<br><br><br><b> 6.) THE VILLAIN. BECAUSE YOU KNEW THIS WAS COMING:</b> So have you had time to go back to your book and remember Lokesh? We good now? You know who he is? <br><br>Yes, you're right. He IS the hundreds of years old villain who wanted to kill Ren and Kishan's father and marry their mother. You remember that part? Now, you remember that he now wants to marry KELSEY, right? Because THAT's so original. <br><br>I'm getting Dust Land flashbacks. It's not pretty. <br><br>Oh, sorry (thanks for the correction, Abby) he doesn't want to marry her just to marry her, he wants a son. Yep. Okay. Great. Because we certainly needed that there. This reminds me of yet another series that tanked. Really hard. By Cassandra Clare. If you don't know what I'm talking about, then consider yourself lucky. VERY lucky. Please, don't go looking for it. You'll only hurt yourself. <br><br>Another note to new authors: Please. No "I MUST HAVE A SON" obsessed villains, please. And if you MUST have them, at least don't make them want to marry the heroine in order to GET said son. You'll notice I said please twice. I'm getting desperate here. Help. Me. <br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>BONUS TIME!!!</b> So, in an attempt to (maybe??) COMPLIMENT the book, I think Kirkus Reviews did a pretty good job of summing up what reading the book is like "shocking, heart-rendin, soul-tearing..." Ye-ap....This thing tore my soul out all right. And stomped on it. And killed my laugh box. And by the end, I was wondering why stuff like this ever gets printed. <br><br><br><b>BONUS TIME OVERTIME!!!!</b> A quote from my lovely cousin to describe these books: "I got it--Kelsey is a ball of yarn being batted around between two cats."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428718i/858100.gif" width="479" height="407" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Yep. Yeah, that pretty much sums it up. Good job Abs. <br><br>And now another quote from a different source (no, not me. What sort of ego-maniac do you think I AM?): "It's a Spanish soap opera!"<br><br>Yes. Yes it is. Now kill it with fire. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428718ra/858102.gif" width="320" height="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4021109602220430232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34403359?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34403359?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34403359?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1341694324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5802962813722443623">4.5/5<br/><br/>Plot<br/>Kelsey and her tigers continue their search on how to break the curse. They are sent to get information on one of Durga's prized possessions. Lokesh is now more determined to find and get Kelsey for his personal reasons that had existed when Ren and Kishan were younger and their parents still alive. In the meantime, Ren and Kishan are bent on showing Kelsey their love for her and that she should make the choice of who to be with.<br/><br/>The Love Triangle<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437659773i/15610390.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I wasn't particularly pleased to see the </span>
  <span id="freeText5802962813722443623" style="display:none">4.5/5<br><br>Plot<br>Kelsey and her tigers continue their search on how to break the curse. They are sent to get information on one of Durga's prized possessions. Lokesh is now more determined to find and get Kelsey for his personal reasons that had existed when Ren and Kishan were younger and their parents still alive. In the meantime, Ren and Kishan are bent on showing Kelsey their love for her and that she should make the choice of who to be with.<br><br>The Love Triangle<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437659773i/15610390.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wasn't particularly pleased to see the love triangle forming but it was okay. It caused a little too much drama for my taste. I thought that Houck should have focused more on the problem at hand but a little romance was okay.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432560560ra/14981820.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Picture the girl watching as a guy<br><br>Characters<br><br>The characters were overall good.<br><br>Kelsey<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437659773i/15610391.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kelsey is a smart and resourceful young lady in this series. In this book, though, she seems to be more dependent on the guy. I wish to have seen her be more independent and possibly have less drama. She was in love and loving two guys but she should just make the decision of what to do.<br><br>Ren<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437659773i/15610392.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ren had amnesia and it affected his love life with Kelsey. The entire time I was wishing for him to just remember her since I know that they are meant to be together. He is handsome, romantic, funny, and protective. He cares a lot for Kelsey and wants to protect her.<br><br>Kishan<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437659773i/15610393._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kishan is and has been in love with Kelsey. He is jealous of Ren and that he still has her affections. He is funny, relaxed, and wants Kelsey to be happy with either decision that she makes.<br><br>The Ending<br><br>There is a definite cliff hanger and I can't wait to get the fourth book when it comes out of hard back. You should read it.</span>

<div id="review_238328994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238328994" />
    <a title="Ceren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6450420-ceren"><img alt="Ceren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317180261p2/6450420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238328994?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceren" href="/user/show/6450420-ceren">Ceren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444734645" href="/book/show/12080697-tiger-s-voyage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6450420-ceren?shelf=avoid-all-costs">avoid-all-costs</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238328994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5593633939981130821">WORST. BOOK. EVER 'eye twitches'....honestly if you like to read good YA with strong heroine, no annoying love rectangles (yes, that's right RECTANGLES, because overall kelsy has had SEVEN guys fall head over heels for her throughout the three books...yep, prehaps in a perfect world I can swallow this BUT SEVEN? why exactly? she consistently comes across an annoying, whiny, twelve year old stuck in an eighteen year old's body) THEN AVOID THIS BOOK AT ALL COSTS!<br/>On top of that, for nearly 250 page</span>
  <span id="freeText5593633939981130821" style="display:none">WORST. BOOK. EVER 'eye twitches'....honestly if you like to read good YA with strong heroine, no annoying love rectangles (yes, that's right RECTANGLES, because overall kelsy has had SEVEN guys fall head over heels for her throughout the three books...yep, prehaps in a perfect world I can swallow this BUT SEVEN? why exactly? she consistently comes across an annoying, whiny, twelve year old stuck in an eighteen year old's body) THEN AVOID THIS BOOK AT ALL COSTS!<br />On top of that, for nearly 250 pages of the book there was NO ACTION WHATSOEVER! All kelsy complained of was 'hmm which brother should I choose next?..'I love ren', <br />2 pages later- I hate Ren I want Kishan, <br />4 pages later- I want Ren again, I want Kishan as a friend, <br />6 pages later- I want Kishan, I want Ren as a friend only, <br />8 pages later- I want Ren while I'm making out with Kishan<br />10 pages later- I want Ren and Kishan<br />11 pages- Ren and I are soulmates (but i'll just casually date Kishan)<br />I KID YOU NOT, SHE CONSISTENTLY DATES, MAKES-OUT AND BREAKS UP WITH BOTH WHILE WONDERING WHICH ONE IS HER 'SOUL MATE'...GRRRR! <br />honestly I could keep up with Kim kardasian's love life better then I could keep up with kelsy's whininess and selfiness. <br />Furthermore, while she's juggling these two (as well as an random scuba diver, OOPS I FORGOT TO MENTION ANOTHER PERSON WHOSE HELPLESSLY IN LOVE WITH HER FOR NO GOOD REASON), the only purpose she serves throughout the whole novel is playing the helpless DAMSEL IN DISTRESS WHILE TWO MEN FIGHT OVER HER...WHY YOU MAY ASK? BECAUSE COLEEN HOUCK SEEMS TO THINK ALL WOMEN ARE HELPLESS FEMALES WAITING TO BE RESCUED! grrrr honestly and here i was thinking stephanie meyer was bad!i RECOMMEND THIS TO NOOO ONE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5593633939981130821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_186579972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186579972" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3460706-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368511566p2/3460706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186579972?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/3460706-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781402784057" href="/book/show/12044735-tiger-s-voyage">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone whose read the previous two. </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lindsay by: </span>
      I did
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3460706-lindsay?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186579972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16173514593748405861">I wanted to absorb all that I read for a few days before reviewing this book. So here it is my official review.<br/><br/>I loved it. I loved the action packed adventures. The way Colleen describes the details makes it so easy to "see" the kraken and the dragons. The emotional writing makes me love, hate and envy the characters-- which is why it took me a week before I could write this review. I know Colleen won't lead me astray, and I now long to know the next chapter in the story. I don't want to post an</span>
  <span id="freeText16173514593748405861" style="display:none">I wanted to absorb all that I read for a few days before reviewing this book. So here it is my official review.<br /><br />I loved it. I loved the action packed adventures. The way Colleen describes the details makes it so easy to "see" the kraken and the dragons. The emotional writing makes me love, hate and envy the characters-- which is why it took me a week before I could write this review. I know Colleen won't lead me astray, and I now long to know the next chapter in the story. I don't want to post any spoilers so I'll simply say I am and will always be Team Ren. Kesley, Mr. Kadam, Durga and Phet remain my favorite insightful writing by Mrs. Houck. I identify strongly with Kelsey's sense of self and dedication to the journey ahead and her extreme loyalty( again -- still Team Ren). Mr. Kadam is less apart of this book than the previous two, so I savored the times he was shared with us. I am so glad he got to go into Durga's temple this time. I feel like it was such an honor for him to be a part of that experience, I was so excited for him. And Phet- I love this crazy little old man. His wisdom how ever strangely delivered is fabulously on target and I loved his interactions with the brothers. Oh the boys-- I personally married a Kishan, so I love him for his careful, watchful, thoughtful, trust in Kelsey, he is such a deeper character than we've seen in the last two installments. His support and unfailing love for our girl is breathtaking at times. Oh Ren- I loved you from your first hello, and at times in this book its a good thing your fictional because I wanted to shake you until you'd snap out of it, and stop with the standoffish behavior and the flaunting of the floozy???seriously!! Alas though when it came down to those final chapters and the tears were streaming down my face - the tears were for you dear Ren. Everything I know will be fully explained in books to come and it's hard to understand right now the why's, but I have faith. Super powered golden lightening has to mean something more right??<br /><br />In closing I am such a huge fan of Mrs. Houck's books and her way with her characters that I couldn't not love it more thoroughly than I do. Being able to read it ahead of schedule was and honor and a privilege I can't thank you enough for Colleen. <br /><br /><br />Merged review:<br /><br />I wanted to absorb all that I read for a few days before reviewing this book. So here it is my official review.<br /><br />I loved it. I loved the action packed adventures. The way Colleen describes the details makes it so easy to "see" the kraken and the dragons. The emotional writing makes me love, hate and envy the characters-- which is why it took me a week before I could write this review. I know Colleen won't lead me astray, and I now long to know the next chapter in the story. I don't want to post any spoilers so I'll simply say I am and will always be Team Ren. Kesley, Mr. Kadam, Durga and Phet remain my favorite insightful writing by Mrs. Houck. I identify strongly with Kelsey's sense of self and dedication to the journey ahead and her extreme loyalty( again -- still Team Ren). Mr. Kadam is less apart of this book than the previous two, so I savored the times he was shared with us. I am so glad he got to go into Durga's temple this time. I feel like it was such an honor for him to be a part of that experience, I was so excited for him. And Phet- I love this crazy little old man. His wisdom how ever strangely delivered is fabulously on target and I loved his interactions with the brothers. Oh the boys-- I personally married a Kishan, so I love him for his careful, watchful, thoughtful, trust in Kelsey, he is such a deeper character than we've seen in the last two installments. His support and unfailing love for our girl is breathtaking at times. Oh Ren- I loved you from your first hello, and at times in this book its a good thing your fictional because I wanted to shake you until you'd snap out of it, and stop with the standoffish behavior and the flaunting of the floozy???seriously!! Everything I know will be fully explained in books to come and it's hard to understand right now the why's, but I have faith. Super powered golden lightening has to mean something more right??<br /><br />In closing I am such a huge fan of Mrs. Houck's books and her way with her characters that I couldn't not love it more thoroughly than I do. Being able to read it ahead of schedule was and honor and a privilege I can't thank you enough for Colleen.</span>
